‚ÄçBen Stott, Managing Director of APWIL added;"I am extremely proud to lead our team of talented and dedicated professionals into its new home with Capital International. From our initial interactions with their leadership team, it was obvious that we share a belief in exceptional client delivery, alongside innovative investment solutions. It is exciting to expand our offering for our existing and future clients, who will also benefit from access to Capital‚Äôs market leading technology."

‚ÄçAnthony Long, Chairman of Capital International Group:"We‚Äôve admired APW Investors for some time, not only for their investment expertise, but also for their leadership in sustainability and commitment to the community. 31. Supernova calls for private equity to expand ‚Äòtimid‚Äô foray into deeptech

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ More capital key for European deeptech to scale-up
‚Ä¢ Sponsor's EUR 100m fund targets 20 deals
‚Ä¢ Seeks to expand LP base beyond mostly-France in future

Details:
Although private equity is investing more in European deeptech, its ‚Äútimid‚Äù foray is not creating sufficient capital for companies in the sector to scale-up, managing partner Pierre-Emmanuel Struyven and investment director at Supernova Invest Micha√´l Thomas said.

‚ÄòDeeptech‚Äô, or ‚Äòdeep technology‚Äô, companies offer innovative solutions based on groundbreaking scientific research. The sector can refer to artificial intelligence (AI) and machine learning, as well as quantum computing, biotechnology or robotics.

When Supernova was established in 2017, it was one of the few European deeptech pure-players in the venture capital market alongside Omnes Capital and Jolt Capital, Struyven said.

New players have progressively emerged, but they mostly focus on funding early-stage companies, he said.

The goal is now to support future market leaders, but that requires more exits to materialise, one of the major issues faced by deeptech investors today, he said.

A key challenge for early-stage investors is finding buyers or additional investors for their investments at the necessary multiples, Thomas said. An issue especially relevant considering the limited capital from larger funds flowing into the sector.

The ‚Äúclassic‚Äù M&A deal is not the only path, he said, adding that larger funds could join the capital structure and replace early-stage investors on the board.

He named Exotec, a French robotics company, and AI expert Dataiku as companies that saw larger funds taking over historic venture capital investors.

In 2022, Exotec raised ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0UsFu4zoM_Brr5oAiJdk-6JA0L319QPMu7iG5yRLdqHVsr6wUbb9-kXSx6B72QoAEhzODofOXFJenhdNDsHqz0ajWWNab9bZUCqBs7rZNKXEjNdaygtoIN89D9C7HabTjlGP_q1mETzFziu5ft5wsKQ9V52WoeqpqHSoDva6cAYWd6mQj_GXIl8R3U2DLY3m_EcEGoM6IEJfZZX_isHWZLQLqEkyJ1IIpaK3VraxI0VGwlZUGY6RplODxzQ7xjcXJhk6GqpahblD1FffeuL6G3mnpZB1Iini7CwYJjFZarVSDoKmvHTVdJYkKBWdOz5zOLr1yXvnpLOLS8pJt74aFxWBPOc9LQesCdwXu_tiO0-hGN3zk6JcrtMCdn8bMYy5wJwGAGq2pFuer0Ydg_28f8Ng-6WP7qPd4oOPLP3R8OajH-_1wwCe5f3n93H_-Fw_ta0HbL1j7MbMN8ZmXLOY0hYvP9ruI67CPA1-TbTp0QWsXGjAAINF4AkTx48Lp4xaYAU8ckBlQN7VETcZ71ZFTjYdO9iJZN4bEyypxfC4XfzrHkAsFJ07ufXYpj5xuXkW2v5kL2v6VO_N5Hly-6vsuu8z8nsXl6yURQBqqSIs3iz8DAAD__ygE1mE ) USD 335m in a Series D round which valued the business at USD 2bn and led by Goldman Sachs Asset Management.

The same year, Dataiku ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0UsFu4zoM_Brr5oAiJdk-6JA0L319QPMu7iG5yRLdqHVsr6wUbb9-kXSx6B72QoAEhzODofOXFJenhdNDsHqz0ajWWNab9bZUCqBs7rZNKXEjNdaygtoIN89D9C7HabTjlGP_q1mETzFziu5ft5wsKQ9V52WoeqpqHSoDva6cAYWd6mQj_GXIl8R3U2DLY3m_EcEGoM6IEJfZZX_isHWZLQLqEkyJ1IIpaK3VraxI0VGwlZUGY6RplODxzQ7xjcXJ1rI2gakG2fk6cB1MZWRDwJ5qE1Qt4u0uGCQwWmm1Ug2Cpr521HSVJCoUnDk9czq79Mp55aeziEvLS7a9GxYWgz3lPC8FrQvcFbj7YztOoxvd8JGjX67QAnd-GjOPucCdBCDVNBpJnK9GH4L9v33AY_ukj-2j3uOBji__0PHloB7v98MBn-T-5fVz__lfPLSvBW2_YO3HzDbEZ16ymNMULj7b7yKuwz4OfE226dAFrV1owACAROMJEMWPC6ePW2AGPHFAZkDd1BI1Ge9VR041HjrZi2TdGBIvq8TxuVz86RxDLhScOLn32aU8crp5Fdn-Zi5o-1fuzOd5cPmq77vsMvN7Fpevl0QAaagiLd4s_gwAAP__8-7VtQ ) secured USD 200m in a Series F funding round led by new investor Wellington Management, at a USD 3.7bn valuation.

Fifteen deals to go

This February, Supernova raised EUR 100m for its early-stage deeptech fund Supernova Innovation 3, the successor of EUR 75m vehicle Supernova 2, Stryuven said.

Supernova‚Äôs historic investors - CEA Investissement, Cr√©dit Agricole, Bpifrance, bioM√©rieux, Vinci and Michelin - are among Supernova Innovation 3‚Äôs LPs, he said. The vehicle also attracted MACSF as a new investor, he said, adding that around 70% of the fund‚Äôs EUR 100m hard cap came from institutional investors.

The firm aims to expand its LP base, which is mostly French today, to the broader European market, Struyven said.

Supernova started to market its fund in mid-2023, Struyven said, adding that the vehicle‚Äôs LPs were attracted by the firm‚Äôs investment strategy, its deeptech expertise and track record.

Supernova Innovation 3 will pursue around 20 deals, Struyven said. It will deploy in seed or Series A funding rounds and reinvest on average twice in the same business, he added.

The vehicle will pursue two to three deals annually and deploy EUR 1.5m-EUR 2m initially, and up to EUR 7m per portfolio company in total, he said.

It will target European businesses, he said, adding that Supernova has invested in France, Switzerland, the UK, Italy, Denmark, Belgium and Israel. Over the last 18 to 24 months, Supernova invested as much in France as in the rest of Europe, Thomas added.

Supernova Innovation 3 has already invested in five companies: quantum microelectronics expert Quobly ( Profitability is not the only criteria

Supernova deploys in spacetech, digital tech, cleantech, industrial tech and healthtech, Struyven said.

It has lately looked into several software-enabled hardware, including physical AI and autonomous robotics, Thomas said, adding that the firm invested ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0Uk1v4zoM_DXWzQFFfdg66JA0L319QPMu7iG5yRLdqHVsr6QUbX_9Iuli0T3shQAJDmcGQ-cvKeanTOkhWLXZKJRrrNvNeltLCVCbu62pOW64wpY30GrmlmWM3pU4T3aaSxx-NZn5FAul6P51-WSF9ND0nodmEE2rQqNhUI3TILGXPTfMX8ZySXQ3B7I01fcbFmwA0WsWYl5c8ScKW1fIIqCqQdcoOtCVWCt5KyshxZGR5Y0Crbk2ktH0Zsf4RuxkB1BODQENB06knTScyA1GDko0bSNYvN0FjQK0kkqupEFQYmidMH3DhagknCk9Uzq79Epl5eczi7mjXOzgxkxstKdSllyJdYW7Cnd_bMd5cpMbP0r0-QqtcOfnqdBUKtxxAMll00hg56vRh2D_7x7w2D2pY_eo9ngQx5d_xPHlIB_v9-MBn_j-5fVz__lfPHSvldh-wbqPhWyIz5QLW9IcLr7Y7yKuwyGOdE3W9OiCUi4Y0ADAUXsBiOzHhdLHLTANXlBAIkBlWo5KaO9lL5w0Hno-sGTdFBLlVaL4XGd_OsdQKgknSu59calMlG5eWbG_mSux_St3ofMyunLV9112Xei9sMvXSyIA16IRir1Z_BkAAP__hCrWAg ) into Zurich-based ANYbotics, an AI-focused robotic inspection solutions company, last December.

When it comes to pure-player software providers, Supernova is attentive to cloud-based, cybersecurity and vertical AI solutions, which are software platforms tailored for a specific industry, he said.

The AI market is ‚Äúquick‚Äù and very capex-intensive but Supernova is keen on investing in the sector and has done so with Gleamer ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0Uj1v4zoQ_DViJ2O5_JBYsLDj57w8IH6NUtgdRa5iJrKkI-kgya8_2DkccsU1BLjY2ZnZWecvKeanTOkhWLXZKJRrrNvNeltLCVCbu62pOW64wpY30GrmlmWM3pU4T3aaSxx-fTLzKRZK0f3r8skK6aHpPQ_NIJpWhUbDoBqnQWIve26Yv4zlkuhuDmRpqu83LNgAotcsxLy44k8Utq6QRUBVg65RdKArsVby9qyEFEdGljcKtObaSEbTmx3jG7GT1YNutQQTwmAG1Tem6UlAQ9IL03L0LN7mgkYBWkklV9IgKDG0Tpi-4UJUEs6UnimdXXqlsvLzmcXcUS52cGMmNtpTKUuuxLrCXYW7P7rjPLnJjR8l-nyFVrjz81RoKhXuOIBQpkFj2Plq9CHY_7sHPHZP6tg9qj0exPHlH3F8OcjH-_14wCe-f3n93H_-Fw_dayW2X7DuYyEb4jPlwpY0h4sv9ruIa3GII12TNT26oJQLBjQAcNReACL7caH0cQtMgxcUkAhQXVekhPZe9sJJ46HnA0vWTSFRXiWKz3X2p3MMpZJwouTeF5fKROnmlRX7m7kS279yFzovoytXfd9l14XeC7t8nSQCcC0aodibxZ8BAAD__2IV1fY ) in June 2023, he added.

On average, Supernova aims to exit a company after five to seven years when it entered during a seed funding round or Series A, and between three to six years after a Series B, Thomas said.

The firm aims for a two-digit IRR for this vehicle that is well above 10%, Struyven said. Profitability adds value to a company, but it is not the only criterion for investors looking for strong growth, which is reassuring for the venture capital market, Thomas added.

Supernova has more than EUR 800m assets under management (AUM) and plans to reach EUR 1bn AUM next year, Struyven said. It has invested in around 100 companies in total, he added.

It also has an agrifood fund, launched in 2023, which has carried ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0UsFu4zoM_Brr5oAiJdk-6JA0L319QPMu7iG5yRLdqHVsr6wUbb9-kXSx6B72QoAEhzODofOXFJenhdNDsHqz0ajWWNab9bZUCqBs7rZNKXEjNdaygtoIN89D9C7HabTjlGP_q1mETzFziu5ft5wsKQ9V52WoeqpqHSoDva6cAYWd6mQj_GXIl8R3U2DLY3m_EcEGoM6IEJfZZX_isHWZLQLqEkyJ1IIpaK3VraxI0VGwlZUGY6RplODxzQ7xjcXJGlRVTx4b0zeKOkdEoCuqJXcde2YRb3fBIIHRSquVahA09bWjpqskUaHgzOmZ09mlV84rP51FXFpesu3dsLAY7CnneSloXeCuwN0f23Ea3eiGjxz9coUWuPPTmHnMBe4kAJmqQi3F-Wr0Idj_2wc8tk_62D7qPR7o-PIPHV8O6vF-PxzwSe5fXj_3n__FQ_ta0PYL1n7MbEN85iWLOU3h4rP9LuI67OPA12SbDl3Q2oUGDABINJ4AUfy4cPq4BWbAEwdkBtRNLVGT8V515FTjoZO9SNaNIfGyShyfy8WfzjHkQsGJk3ufXcojp5tXke1v5oK2f-XOfJ4Hl6_6vssuM79ncfl6SQSQhirS4s3izwAAAP__biLV_w ) out three investments so far with a fourth underway, he said, declining to give further details.

The firm has 33 people, including about 20 among its investment team, he said.

32. Thyssenkrupp shareholders to vote on 49% TKMS spin-off at 8 August EGM - report (translated)

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Unresolved financing questions amid talks with federal government
‚Ä¢ Federal government role not yet clarified, Ministry of Defence declines comment
‚Ä¢ Shareholders expected to approve 49% TKMS spin-off

Details:
Thyssenkrupp shareholders are to vote on the minority spin-off of its naval division, Thyssenkrupp Marine Systems (TKMS), before the end of the year, Handelsblatt reported.

Without citing a specific source, the German daily said shareholders are expected to approve the 49% spin-off at an EGM on 8 August.

Company sources noted there were still unresolved questions regarding the financing of the project, and added that the role of the federal government has not yet been clarified.

The report said ThyssenKrupp confirmed to the Bild newspaper that it is "in intensive negotiations with the federal government."

The German Ministry of Defence declined to comment on the matter when asked, the report added.

The original article was published today (23 June) on page 20.

33. Sidenor makes its entry into Talgo conditional on SEPI entering into shareholding

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ SEPI's stake to aid Talgo's EUR 400m debt refinancing with creditor banks

Details:
Sidenor has made its entry into Spain-based railway manufacturer Talgo conditional on SEPI's participation in the capital, El Periodico reported, citing sources familiar with the negotiations.

The aim of Jos√© Antonio Jainaga, president of the steel company, is that state-owned SEPI takes a stake of at least 5%, although the target percentage would be 10%, the item said.

With the backing of the state in the shareholding, Talgo would have greater credibility among the pool of more than twenty creditor banks to an enventual refinancing of its more than EUR 400m of debt, the report said.

Sidenor and official sources from SEPI declined to comment on the information, the item noted.

Jainaga's intention is not to close the pre-agreement signed on 14 February until it has been clarified and the groundwork has been laid to resolve the troubled financial situation that Talgo is going through, El Periodico report added.

As reported, Sidenor, has a pre-agreement with the British fund Trilantic to acquire up to 29.7% of the manufacturer Talgo with the backing  of the Basque Government and two banking foundations.

As reported, SEPI has made its entry into Talgo conditional to securing significant management influence, including getting at least one board seat.

34. Hueller Hille owner faces sale pressure from trade union (translated)

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Insolvency proceedings seen as only solution by IG Metall representative
‚Ä¢ CEO disputes insolvency need despite significant liabilities
‚Ä¢ Huelle Hille faces low employee turnout and substantial two-digit million Euro debt

Details:
The owner of Hueller Hille, a German machine tool manufacturer, is facing pressure from trade union IG Metall to sell the company, Muenchner Merkur reported.

The German-language newspaper quoted IG Metall representative Thomas Bohlender as saying that Hueller Hille is in a dire situation that can only be resolved by insolvency proceedings. He explained that IG Metall wants the Hueller Hille management to pave the way for new investors.

Bingcheng Zhang, the CEO and backer of Hueller Hille, has meanwhile claimed that there was no need to file for insolvency, the report said.

The piece mentioned unconfirmed reports of Hueller Hille having amassed a two-digit million euro sum in liabilities. Only a fraction of the 170 employees are currently turning up for work, it added.

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Deal saves 50 jobs at German industrial processing solutions developer
‚Ä¢ Wang brings metalworking industry expertise and Chinese customer network
‚Ä¢ SAMAG Machine Tools had EUR 14.1m turnover before rescue

Details:
SAMAG Machine Tools, a German industrial processing solutions developer under administration, has struck a rescue deal with Austrian entrepreneur Wei Wang, a press release stated.

The German-language statement said that the creditors have already proved the transaction. It pointed out that the deal saves 50 of 90 jobs at SAMAG Machine Tools.

Wang grew up in Austria as the son of Chinese parents and hails from a family of entrepreneurs in the metalworking industry, the release noted. As a former partner of auditing firm PwC in Germany, he has overseen a number of successful acquisitions in the mechanical engineering sector.

The statement highlighted that Wang has been working as an investor and entrepreneur in the industry since 2019 and has an extensive network of potential customers in China.

SAMAG Machine Tools manufactures machine tools for metal cutting, primarily multi-spindle horizontal CNC machining centres, as well as deep drilling and vertical milling machines, the announcement stated. The company‚Äôs most recent turnover was around EUR 14.1m.

SAMAG Machine Tools, which had initially hoped to restructure itself under self-administration, had hired Thorsten Springstub of law firm Tiefenbacher and Simon Leopold of ABG Consulting-Partner as restructuring counsels, as previously reported ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0Uk1v2zAM_TXWzQFFfUUHHZJm6Tqg2cU9JDdZohu1ju3JStH01w9Jh6E77EKABB_fe3j04ZzT_DRTfohOrdcK5Qrr5Xq1qaUEqO3dxtYc11zhkhtYauanqU_BlzQObhhL6v40Mws5FcrJf_fz0QkZwLSBR9MJs1TRaOiU8RoktrLlloVzX86Z7sZIjob6fs2iiyBazWKaJ1_CkeLGF3IIqGrQNYoGdCVWSt7KQkhxYOS4UaA111YyGt5cn96IHZ3oDGFH2FpjOm1Ma6GzKKRpQ5BWeZZud0GjAK2kkgtpEZToll7Y1nAhKgknys-UTz6_UlmE8cTS3NBcXOf7mVjvjqVMcyVWFW4r3P6zncbBD76_lBTmK7TCbRiHQkOpcMsBJDdaSslOV6MP0f1sHvDQPKlD86h2uBeHl2_i8LKXj_e7fo9PfPfy-rH7-JH2zWslNp-w5jKRi-mZ5sKmPMZzKO6riOuwSz1dk7Ut-qiUjxY0AHDUQQAi-3WmfLkFpiEIikgEqOySoxI6BNkKL22AlncsOz_ETPMiU3qu53A8pVgqCUfK_n3yuQyUb15ZcX-ZK7H5L3eh09T7ctX3VXZd6L2w8-dLIgDXwgjF3hz-DgAA__-h8dYV ) .

37. thyssenkrupp EGM approves spin-off of TKMS 49%, extends CEO Miguel L√≥pez's contract by five years

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ To list TKMS on Frankfurt Stock Exchange this calendar year
‚Ä¢ CEO Miguel L√≥pez's contract extended by five years until 31 May 2031
‚Ä¢ thyssenkrupp AG presents future strategic target model for independent business units

Details:
Supervisory Board of thyssenkrupp AG approves Executive Board‚Äôs plans for a stand-alone solution for the marine business ‚Äì Miguel L√≥pez‚Äôs CEO contract extended by five years

*

Supervisory Board recommends that the shareholders approve the spin-off of a 49 percent minority interest in Marine Systems at an extraordinary general meeting

*

Resolution planned at extraordinary general meeting on August 8, 2025 ‚Äì aim is to list Marine Systems (TKMS) on the Frankfurt Stock Exchange within this calendar year

*

Independence should boost the competitiveness and growth opportunities of TKMS

*

Executive Board presents its future strategic target model for the further development of the group as a whole

*

Top management focuses on continuity in the strategic transformation and improvement in the competitiveness of the company‚Äôs businesses

*

Supervisory Board agrees to extend the contract of the CEO of thyssenkrupp AG, Miguel √Ångel L√≥pez Borrego, by five years until May 31, 2031

thyssenkrupp is committed to consistently pressing ahead with the spin-off of the Marine Systems segment (TKMS). At an extraordinary meeting, the Supervisory Board of thyssenkrupp AG today approved the Executive Board‚Äôs plans to spin off of a minority interest in TKMS. The positioning as a stand-alone listed company should boost the competitiveness and growth opportunities of TKMS in the long term.

The plans involve consolidating the marine business under a new holding company and transferring 49 percent of the TKMS shares to the shareholders of thyssenkrupp AG in proportion to their interest in thyssenkrupp AG. This would make the shareholders of thyssenkrupp AG direct shareholders of TKMS. Through the spin-off, 51 percent ‚Äì and hence the majority interest ‚Äì of TKMS remain with thyssenkrupp AG. TKMS thus remains a fully consolidated company in the thyssenkrupp Group. The shareholders of thyssenkrupp AG will be asked to approve the plan at an extraordinary general meeting on August 8, 2025. The aim is to finalize the listing of TKMS on the Frankfurt Stock Exchange within this calendar year.

Prof. Siegfried Russwurm, Chairman of the Supervisory Board of thyssenkrupp AG: ‚ÄúTKMS is proof that Germany can set standards worldwide in cutting-edge technologies. The Supervisory Board of thyssenkrupp AG is convinced that TKMS will be best able to exploit the huge growth potential as a global pioneer in the maritime defense industry as an independent entity. We therefore recommend that the shareholders of thyssenkrupp AG approve the spin-off of TKMS at the extraordinary general meeting.‚Äù

As the world market leader for non-nuclear submarines, TKMS is one of the leading system providers in the maritime defense industry. With an order backlog at a record level of around 18 billion euros, production at the company will be at full capacity well into the next decade. The long-term geostrategic developments also provide the company with further growth opportunities that will be best leveraged through this independence.

The planned spin-off is consistent with the group‚Äôs strategic realignment. thyssenkrupp AG is basically aiming in the medium term to become a strategic holding company with autonomous units, while retaining majority stakes in the businesses. Similar steps were already taken in the past, such as floating the hydrogen subsidiary thyssenkrupp nucera on the stock market.

Future strategic target model for the further development of the group presented

At the extraordinary meeting of the Supervisory Board, the Executive Board of thyssenkrupp AG also presented the current status of its future strategic target model for the further development of the group as a whole, parts of which had become known prematurely in May. The main goal of this strategy is to gradually turn all business units at thyssenkrupp into independent companies and open them up to third-party involvement. Important steps toward this goal have already been taken with the spin-off of a minority interest of Marine Systems at a well-advanced stage and the initiated efforts to create a 50/50 joint venture of Steel Europe with EPG.

Over the coming years, efforts will be made to achieve capital market readiness for the Materials Services and Automotive Technology segments as well and then to make them independent. The relatively young Decarbon Technologies segment is also to be made independent in the future, as soon as the necessary requirements have been met and the market for green technologies permits it. thyssenkrupp AG basically intends to retain a majority stake in the businesses once they have achieved capital market readiness. The goal is to form a focused, agile, and realigned industrial group: thyssenkrupp AG as the strategic holding company with strong, independent businesses.

Contract for CEO Miguel √Ångel L√≥pez Borrego extended by five years

At today‚Äôs extraordinary meeting, the Supervisory Board also agreed to extend the contract of the CEO of thyssenkrupp AG, Miguel √Ångel L√≥pez Borrego, by five years until May 31, 2031. Mr. L√≥pez‚Äôs current contract ends at the end of May 2026.

The group is undergoing a challenging and urgently needed transformation process, in which reliability, leadership and clear priorities are of the essence. The extension of Miguel L√≥pez‚Äôs contract is an expression of our confidence in his leadership and our conviction that clear orientation and continuity along the chosen path are crucial to the further progress and future of thyssenkrupp.‚Äù

38. Micropower Group acquires LEAB Automotive

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Acquisition expands Micropower's technological capabilities in electrification
‚Ä¢ Fieldfisher, Setterwalls (legal) advised Micropower
‚Ä¢ Micropower is backed by Polaris

Details:
Sweden-based Micropower Group has acquired German mobile power specialist LEAB Automotive.

Financial terms of the deal were not disclosed.

Fieldfisher advises Swedish Micropower Group AB on acquisition of German LEAB Automotive GmbH

Locations

European law firm Fieldfisher has provided comprehensive legal advice to Sweden-based Micropower Group AB on its acquisition of German mobile power specialist LEAB Automotive GmbH. The transaction, which strengthens Micropower's position in the electrification and mobile energy solutions market, involved full-service legal support across corporate, regulatory, employment, tax, intellectual property, and real estate matters.

With this transaction, Micropower transforms a trusted distribution partnership of over 25 years into a fully integrated group structure. The acquisition supports Micropower's strategic objective to expand its technological capabilities and strengthen its position in the electrification market. By integrating LEAB into the group, Micropower enhances its ability to deliver system-based power solutions for complex vehicle applications ‚Äì particularly in emergency services, utility, and industrial transportation sectors.

Micropower Group, headquartered in V√§xj√∂, Sweden, is a leading European manufacturer of battery systems, power supplies, and charging solutions for industrial use. With production and logistics sites in Sweden, Finland, and the United States, the company delivers more than 1.2 million units annually.

LEAB Automotive, located in northern Germany, specialises in customised mobile power systems and is recognised across Europe for its engineering expertise and customer-oriented solutions.

Fieldfisher provided comprehensive legal support to Micropower throughout the transaction. üåê INTERNET / ECOMMERCE

39. US buyers pile into UK-listed corporates in 2Q with more deals expected post-summer - Analysis

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Three US strategic-led deals worth GBP 4.7bn announced in 2Q
‚Ä¢ Technology and real estate among sector hotspots

Details:
US buyers are accelerating their pursuit of UK-listed corporates with 2Q25 already among the strongest quarters for transatlantic M&A since 2020, according to Mergermarket data.

This momentum is expected to continue amid ongoing geopolitical tensions, lingering trade tariffs, and appealing UK valuations, with US buyers showing increasing interest in takeovers of London-listed businesses, dealmakers said.

In 2Q25 so far, three deals worth an equity value of GBP 4.7bn have been agreed.

This makes it one of the strongest quarters for US acquisitions of London-listed corporates since the Coronavirus pandemic, exceeded only by 1Q24 (GBP 14.6bn), 3Q21 (GBP 13.9bn) and 4Q20 (GBP 7.1bn).

The total number of UK-listed corporates which have announced deals to be acquired by US buyers in 1H25 is six, at a combined equity value of GBP 6.4bn. This compares to five deals in 1H24 worth GBP 15.4bn, though this includes International Paper's GBP 12.6bn acquisition of DS Smith, which makes up 82% of that period's total deal value.

‚ÄúCompared to this time last year, I‚Äôm encouraged by where we stand,‚Äù said Adrian Beidas, Barclays co-head of UK Investment Banking. ‚ÄúContrary to expectations, market activity has rebounded swiftly, with clients re-engaging far more quickly than we had forecast.‚Äù

And that interest looks set to continue. ‚ÄúI [was] really encouraged by the bounce back in May in terms of M&A dialogue,‚Äù said Citi UK Head of Investment Banking, James Fleming. ‚ÄúThat won‚Äôt translate into public announcements perhaps until after the summer because M&A is a very long tail business.‚Äù

( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0Uk1v4zoM_DXWzYFESnJ80CFpXto-oHlvgfSQ3GSJTtT6ayW5aPvrF04Xi172IkADkjOcoXVzDOk5UXz0Rm23CuQGyvV2syul5Lys73Z1KWArFKxFxdea2WnqgrM5jIMZxhza35_EXAyZYrAPNl0NSserxglftVitla80b1VlNZfQyEbUzM1dniPdjZ4MDeX9lnnjOTaa-ZAmm92V_M5mMsBBlVyXgEeuC9woeXtWKPHMyIhKca2FriWj4c104Y3Y1aCSXlaSQysa8JWtK0Lv6kZQ6xUgsnCbyzUg10oquZI1cIXt2mLdVAKxkLyneKHY2_hKeeXGnoV0pJRNa7tErDPXnKdU4KaAfQF754dV31-cdVdaDZQL2JMPeYzBdqUbh0zDgi0CC9j70c09DbmMNI1pKfv4hhawz_3DD6nE_xOxfnHj0Zv_jo9wPj6r8_FJHeCE55d_8Pxykk_3h-4Ez-Lw8vp5-Pw3nI6vBe6-2o4fExkfLpQym-LoZ5fN970WsA0dLfHXDVivlPU115xzAdohB2A_Z4oft1Q1d0geiDioei1AoXZONmhl7XgjWhaNHXyktIoULmVy1z74XEh-pWjfJxvzQDHdvMzmD3OBu79yZ-qnzuZF33fZZab3zOavuwXOhcYKFXsz8CsAAP__DfnkTA )

Rebalancing between strategic and private equity buyers

A growing number of UK-listed companies are attracting interest from both US strategic buyers and US-based private equity sponsors.

San Francisco-based DoorDash‚Äôs GBP 2.8bn cash offer for food delivery group Deliveroo represents the largest deal announced so far in 2Q. Also announced in 2Q were US semiconductor group Qualcomm‚Äôs GBP 1.8bn offer for Alphawave, and US pawnbroker FirstCash‚Äôs GBP 351m offer for H&T Group.

Not included in the figures for 2Q is a potential offer for Alpha Group by New York-listed Corpay, where no price has been disclosed. Corpay‚Äôs initial approach was rejected, and it now has until 7 July to announce a firm offer for Alpha Group, which has a current market capitalisation of GBP 1.3bn.

‚ÄúThis year, we are seeing a rebalancing towards an even split between US strategic buyers and financial buyers bidding for UK assets,‚Äù said Sonica Tolani, Public M&A Partner at White & Case, who noted that last year‚Äôs activity was mainly driven by private equity.

‚ÄúUS strategics will act when it makes sense,‚Äù added Kate Cooper, M&A Partner at Freshfields. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôve benefited from a strong dollar, solid economic performance, and significant firepower.‚Äù

While not classified as cross-border transactions by Mergermarket data, US financial sponsors have continued to remain active in public-to-private deals on the London market.

Recent examples include Advent and KKR‚Äôs separate approaches for UK instrumentation and control specialist Spectris. KKR‚Äôs proposal has been rejected by Spectris, while its board said it was minded to recommend Advent‚Äôs GBP 3.7bn equity value offer.

Advent has until 7 July to firm up its offer, while KKR has until 11 July to make an offer under UK Put Up or Shut Up (PUSU) rules.

KKR is also vying for UK healthcare REIT Assura.

Together with Stonepeak, KKR has bid GBP 1.7bn for Assura but is facing a competing bid from Assura‚Äôs UK-listed rival Primary Health Properties.

‚ÄúLooking mostly at activity post-summer, I‚Äôm seeing an increase in public-to-privates,‚Äù said Fleming.

‚ÄúThe financial sponsor community have got a lot of capital to commit and we‚Äôre being asked to look at a lot of P2Ps.‚Äù

He added that US private equity firms are specifically looking at companies that have a proportion, or a high proportion, of their earnings from the US and where they think that the asset could relist in the US in a number of years‚Äô time.

Valuation gaps, sector hotspots

Beyond macroeconomic drivers, valuation gaps between UK and US companies are continuing to attract inbound interest.

Although the dollar has depreciated against sterling in recent months, it is still trading at relatively historically high levels, said Patrick Sarch, Head of UK Public M&A at White & Case.

And, while UK equities have performed well recently ‚Äì in particular the FTSE 250, where much of the deal activity is ‚Äì UK corporates continue to trade at much lower multiples than US equivalents, he explained.

‚ÄúThis combination continues to make US inbound acquisitions into the UK attractive,‚Äù Sarch said.

( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0Ur1u4zwQfBqxk7Fc_kgqWNjx53wJLr7GKeyOIlcWE_0dSQdJnv5g53BIcw0BDnZ3ZmfWuksM6TlRfPBGbTYK5RrLerPellIClM3dtik5brjCmldQa2aXZQjO5jBPZppz6P58EnMxZIrB_m9Tb4R0ULWO-6oTVa18paFTldUgsZUtb5i7DPkS6W72ZGgq7zfMGw-i1cyHtNjsevJbm8kgoCpBlygOoAuxVvL2rIQUJ0aGVwq05rqRjKY3M4Q3Yr2pG195qFE1kldSeumx80AkJfeVEx0Lt7mgUYBWUsmVbBCU6GormrbiQhQSRopniqONr5RXbh5ZSAdK2XR2SMQG0-e8pEKsC9wVuHN-Wo3j2VnX02qiXOCOfMhzDHYo3Txlmq7YVWCBOz-7y0hTLiMtc7qWfXxDC9w9Tp_b3Y-O-sDGqxsP3vw8PODp8KxOhye1x6M4vfwnTi9H-XS_H474zPcvr5_7z8dwPLwWYvvVdvhYyPhwppTZEmd_cdl83-sKdmGga_xNi9YrZX0DGgA4aicAkf26UPy4parBCfJIBKiamqMS2jnZCisbBy3vWDR28pHSKlI4l8n1Y_C5kNBTtO-LjXmimG5eZvOXuRDbf3JnGpfB5qu-77LLTO-ZXb7uFgG4FpVQ7M3g7wAAAP__TLfklg )

Cooper pointed out that interest isn‚Äôt limited to the main market.

‚ÄúThere‚Äôs also a lot of interest in AIM companies, which have struggled for many years to attract strong valuations, and investors there are looking for exits," she said.

Dealmakers report strong interest from US buyers across several sectors, particularly technology, real estate, industrials and financial services.

Sarch said he continues to see ‚Äúa high level of interest from US buyers for technology businesses‚Äù and expects this trend to carry on through the rest of the year.

Real estate is another standout sector. The competitive bid battle for UK healthcare landlord Assura demonstrates the appeal of the sector.

Usman Khan, Private Capital Real Assets Partner at McDermott, Will & Emery, said a "confluence of factors‚Äù is driving US interest in UK-listed real estate, including valuations that remain materially discounted to Net Asset Value (NAV) and the foreign-exchange dynamic.

‚ÄúFor platforms with long-income characteristics, like healthcare, logistics or specialist infrastructure, the yield profile is especially appealing in a rate environment that‚Äôs now starting to ease. The UK public real estate sector also offers transparent governance and liquidity not always available elsewhere,‚Äù he said.

Fleming said industrials and financial services are ‚Äúlikely to be the bulk of the focus,‚Äù but emphasised that activity is ‚Äúquite broad‚Äù across various sectors.

by Elisha Juttla, with analytics by William Cain

40. Woody Johnson in advanced talks to buy Crystal Palace stake for GBP 190m - report

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Johnson in talks with John Textor for his 43% stake in target
‚Ä¢ Leads bidding against Florida entertainment major, Jimmy Butler consortium

Details:
Woody Johnson, owner of the New York Jets, is in advanced talks to acquire John Textor's 43% stake in Crystal Palace for an estimated GBP 190m, BBC reported citing insiders close to the matter.

These sources indicated that Johnson is currently ahead of two other parties vying for the stake in Textor's multi-club company, Eagle Football Holdings. However, the deal to acquire stake in the Selhurst Park club is not yet ratified, but is in final stages.

The other bidders for John Textor's stake in Crystal Palace includes a Florida-based entertainment major and a consortium featuring NBA star Jimmy Butler, along with investment vehicle Sportsbank, the BBC report noted.

43. Conrady seeks to acquire companies struggling with succession planning (translated)

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Comprehensive representation sought in Germany, Austria, and Switzerland
‚Ä¢ Conrady's 2024 turnover EUR 119m, mainly from its home market

Details:
Conrady, a family-owned German cleaning services group, is seeking acquisitions, managing partner Thomas Conrady told Frankfurter Allgemeine.

The German-language daily cited Conrady as saying that the goal is to achieve a turnover of EUR 200m, and acquisitions are planned for this purpose. Conrady said he is actively looking for companies that are struggling with succession planning. Conrady said he is aiming for comprehensive representation in Germany, Austria and Switzerland.

The Conrady Group achieved a turnover of EUR 119m in 2024, around three quarters of which was generated in its home market. In addition to cleaning services, the company provides fa√ßade cleaning services using industrial climbers, and drones could also be used to assist with this in future, according to the report.

The original article appeared in print; Page 25

44. Impact Partners acquires minority stake in Grupo Aire Limpio

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ EUR 8m investment supports growth plan
‚Ä¢ Abante advised Impact Partners
‚Ä¢ Grupo Aire Limpio doubles revenue to EUR 17.2m in 2024, has 140+ employees
‚Ä¢ Aura: Automated building monitoring and control solutions.
‚Ä¢ Aire Limpio: Electromechanical systems for ventilation, air purification and filtration.
‚Ä¢ Ambisalud: Indoor air quality (IAQ) control and improvement consultancy.
‚Ä¢ Commtech: Commissioning services for building and mission-critical environments.
‚Ä¢ Acsos: Building certifications (WELL, LEED, BREEAM, DGNB, Verde‚Ä¶).

Details:
Impact Partners acquires a minority stake in Grupo Aire Limpio

The European fund Impact Partners has acquired a minority stake in Grupo Aire Limpio, a Spanish company specializing in environmental wellbeing and sustainability in built environments. Advised by Abante, this capital increase represents an injection of EUR 8m, providing the Group with the necessary resources to accelerate its business growth plan over the next five years.

‚ÄúImpact Partners has fully trusted our strategic plan since the very beginning of the deal, and throughout the process they have consistently emphasized the importance of respecting the autonomy of our project,‚Äù explains Tom√°s Higuero, co-founder and CEO of Grupo Aire Limpio.

As such, the executive partners of the Group will retain the majority stake and continue to lead management across the various business areas in which they operate. Impact Partners‚Äô objective is to support Grupo Aire Limpio in consolidating its position as a leader in services for healthy and sustainable buildings.

With 26 years of history, Grupo Aire Limpio has experienced strong growth since the start of this decade, doubling its revenues to reach EUR 17.2m in 2024, with EBITDA of EUR 2.3m. With over 140 employees, the Group serves more than a thousand clients across 8 countries, with offices in Madrid, Barcelona, and Santiago de Compostela.

‚ÄúWe saw major business opportunities emerging from the profound transformation the real estate sector is undergoing, particularly in the demanding areas of decarbonization, health and wellbeing, and the fight against building obsolescence,‚Äù says Tom√°s Higuero. ‚ÄúAnd since our goal is to be involved throughout the entire lifecycle of various asset types‚Äîhospitals, schools, offices, hotels, data centers, residential, leisure, industrial, healthcare, pharmaceutical industry, logistics, etc.‚Äîscaling up was essential, both organically and inorganically.‚Äù

In this context, the executive shareholders of Grupo Aire Limpio evaluated different partners for this next stage of growth until they found the perfect match in Impact Partners. This European investment fund focuses on companies that contribute to a fair transition toward a decarbonized economy, with special attention to balancing social and economic factors‚Äîa philosophy closely aligned with Grupo Aire Limpio‚Äôs business purpose.

‚ÄúWe see in Aire Limpio a company with a unique positioning in the Spanish market, offering solutions that respond to the new market demands and boasting strong potential for growth and consolidation,‚Äù says Mathieu Cornieti, CEO of Impact Partners. ‚ÄúMore than 50% of the beneficiaries of the company‚Äôs solutions are hospital patients and schoolchildren, which speaks volumes about the Group‚Äôs social impact,‚Äù adds Nicolas Touboulic, Managing Partner of Impact Partners Iberica.

Environmental Wellbeing and Sustainability in Built Environments

Today, the Group operates a highly specialized brand structure‚ÄîAura, Aire Limpio, Ambisalud, Commtech, and ACSOS‚Äîallowing it to cover key areas related to building decarbonization and control, environmental wellbeing of properties, commissioning, optimal performance of systems, audits, validations, and analytics of indoor air and water quality, as well as verification and measurement services for certifications such as WELL, LEED, BREEAM, or DGNB.

Their solutions help buildings and their systems become healthier and more environmentally friendly, while also boosting asset performance to minimize both carbon footprint and operating costs.

ENTER, BREATHE. TAKE CARE AND BE CARED FOR

Founded in 1999, Grupo Aire Limpio is Spain‚Äôs leading company in environmental wellbeing and sustainability for built environments. Its solutions help make buildings and their systems healthier and more environmentally responsible, while boosting performance to minimize both carbon footprint and operating expenses.

Formed by Aura, Aire Limpio, Ambisalud, Commtech, and ACSOS, the Group‚Äôs structure of highly specialized companies allows it to deliver top-quality service across key areas such as building decarbonization and control, environmental wellbeing, commissioning, system performance, indoor air and water quality audits and analyses, and certification services including WELL, LEED, BREEAM, and DGNB.

Currently, the Group monitors over 8,000,000 m¬≤ of office space through its BMS-Retrofit and SMoCAI platforms, while its products and technologies improve health and productivity in more than 600 corporate buildings and over 750 schools, with more than 7,000 SIAV units installed. In healthcare settings, more than 800 isolation environments have been adapted to reduce infection risk, and over 400 hospitals rely on the Group‚Äôs technology to support patient recovery. This is in addition to more than 12,000 air quality inspections in healthcare, corporate, and commercial buildings; over 1,000 commissioning projects ensuring that buildings and data centers meet their design reliability targets; and exclusive rights for WELL audits and certifications (the only authorized PTO in Spain), among others.

Grupo Aire Limpio is also strongly committed to R&D&I as a key differentiator, having invested over EUR 5m in projects developed in collaboration with prestigious Spanish institutions such as CIEMAT, CSIC, and CDTI, among others.

Impact Partners was founded in 2007 with the goal of building a more sustainable and equitable society through entrepreneurship. As a pioneering platform fully dedicated to impact investing, with over ‚Ç¨500 million in assets under management, Impact Partners is now a European leader with offices in Paris, Frankfurt, Copenhagen, Milan, and Barcelona. Through its Impact Growth fund‚Äîan Article 9 fund under the European Sustainable Finance Disclosure Regulation (SFDR)‚ÄîImpact Partners provides both financial and human support.

45. Interest in Evalueserve cools - report (translated)

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Initial private equity interest cools noticeably
‚Ä¢ Evalueserve valued at USD 400m in sale led by Rothschild

Details:
Buyer interest in Evalueserve, a Swiss data and insights analytics service provider, has cooled, Finanz und Wirtschaft reported, citing several people familiar with the situation. The unnamed sources said interest has cooled noticeably due to the increased use of artificial intelligence, which could potentially make the further outsourcing of individual work steps and projects obsolete.

The report said that initially, investors such as Blackstone, Bain Capital and Goldman Sachs were among those interested, while one source said Partners Group had also been interested but had since withdrawn. Possible bidders also include mid-market investors such as Bregal Unternehmerkapital (BU) and Montagu.

Permira, which already owns Evalueserve's competitor Acuity Knowledge Partners, has also looked at the company, the report said.

The report said Rothschild is leading the sale, which values the company at around USD 400m (EUR 347m).

The original article was published in the weekend edition on page 6.

46. Globegarden close to sale to private equity buyer - report (translated)

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Two PE firms compete for acquisition at CHF 200m-300m
‚Ä¢ Houlihan Lokey advises on sale, multiple PE firms interested
‚Ä¢ Globegarden denies sale talk

Details:
Globegarden, the Swiss childcare operator, is close to a sale, Finanz und Wirtschaft, citing unnamed sources.

The Swiss bi-weekly said it had learned from the sources that initial offers have been received. One source said two private equity firms are in the running to acquire the company for a price expected to be between CHF 200m and CHF 300m. The report said Houlihan Lokey has been entrusted with the mandate.

Potential buyers could include Bregal Unternehmerkapital (BU), ICG, Bridgepoint and Cinven, according to the report. The newly founded Jacobs Capital could also be among the interested parties, the report stated.

Partners Group, BU and Houlihan Lokey declined to comment. Globegarden denied sale rumours, stating on request that the company will always remain 100% family-owned.

The original article was published in the weekend edition on page 6.

48. Clarion sale receives lukewarm interest amid valuation gap

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ HK-based PE fund FountainVest still in process
‚Ä¢ PAI, CVC and Ardian not involved, sources say
‚Ä¢ Suitor valuations range from GBP 1.6bn to GBP 2bn

Details:
Blackstone-backed events business Clarion has drawn tepid interest from potential private equity buyers, with some questioning the sellside‚Äôs valuation expectations, according to sources familiar with the matter.

PAI is currently not involved in the process, three sources said. CVC, which had considered teaming up with ICG, has also dropped from the process, two further sources said. Ardian had looked at teaming up with another sponsor, but didn‚Äôt submit a bid either, one source said.

Those three parties, alongside KKR and Hillhouse, were among the sponsors that had reportedly ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0Uk1v4zgM_TXWzQFFfTg66JA0m24XaPbiHpKbLNGNWsf2SnK37a8fJB0MOoe5ECDBx_ceHp1fUsxPmdJDsGq7VSg3WK-3m10tJUBt7nam5rjlCte8gbVmbp6H6F2J02jHqcT-Z5OZT7FQiu5vl89WSA9N53loetGsVWg09KpxGiR2suOG-WUoS6K7KZClsb7fsmADiE6zEPPsij9T2LlCFgFVDbpG0YKuxEbJW1kJKU6MLG8UaM21kYzGNzvEN2Jnyw2iIs4FgpGcekOBB0M99D0PXd-zeLsLGgVoJZVcSYOgRL92wnQNF6KScKH0TOni0iuVlZ8uLOaWcrG9GzKxwZ5LmXMlNhXuK9z_th2n0Y1u-CjR5yu0wr2fxkJjqXDPASRKjdBUYp-nJXmqxG6k_zO7XI0_BPtv-4Cn9kmd2kd1wKM4vfwlTi9H-Xh_GI74xA8vr5-Hz3_isX2txO4L1n7MZEN8plzYnKaw-GK_i7oO-zjQNWnToQtKuWBAAwBH7QUgsv8WSh-3ADV4QQGJAJVZc1RCey874aTx0PGeJevGkCivEsXnOvvzJYZSSThTcu-zS2WkdPPOiv3FXIndH7kLXebBlau-77LrQu-FLV8vigBci0Yo9mbxRwAAAP__8LXb3g ) indicated early interest in the business.

ICG may still be active in the process, two sources said. ICG may seek to be involved as a co-investor, as previously reported ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0Us1u2zwQfBrxJmO5_JF04MGOP-dLgbgX5WDfKHIVM5EllaTSOE9f2CmK9NDLArvY2ZnBrHVLDOkpUXzwRm02CuUay3qz3pZSApTN3bYpOW64wppXUGtm53kIzuYwjWaccuh_N4m5GDLFYP-36WSEdFB1jvuqF1WtfKWhV5XVILGTHW-YW4a8RLqbPBkay_sN88aD6DTzIc02uxP5rc1kEFCVoEsULehCrJW8lZWQ4sjI8EqB1lw3ktH4ZobwRuxkeCWVdSR7ql2nCWqH2ilOWoPoCYGF213QKEArqeRKNghK9LUVTVdxIQoJZ4rPFM82vlJeuenMQmopZdPbIREbzCnnORViXeCuwN1f22Ea7WiHSw4uXaEF7tw0ZhpzgTsOIJEL1WAhdmlaoqNCbEf6mdj5avzBm-_tAx7bJ3VsH9UeD-L48p84vhzk4_1-OOAT37-8fuw_voVD-1qI7SesvcxkfHimlNkcJ7-4bL6Kug77MNA16aZD65WyvgENABy1E4DIfiwUL7cANThBHokAVVNzVEI7JzthZeOg4z2Lxo4-UlpFCs9lcqdz8LmQcKJo32cb80jx5p1l84e5ENt_cmc6z4PNV31fZZeZ3jNbPl8UAbgWlVDszeCvAAAA__-mc9ur ) by the news service.

Hong Kong-based FountainVest is also still in the process, driven perhaps by its interest in Clarion‚Äôs exposure to China, two sources noted.

The sellside, which is advised by Goldman Sachs, expected non-binding bids to be submitted early this week, two sources said. However, bids were still being received mid-week, one of them added.

Some participants have been reaching out to the sellside this week but have yet to receive a process update, two sources said.

According to two of the sources, some potential suitors were valuing the business at an enterprise value of around GBP 1.6bn-GBP 1.75bn ‚Äì well below the GBP 2bn that the sellside was reportedly targeting. Some bids may still have been submitted around the GBP 2bn mark, though, a separate source noted.

Clarion has been marketed off a 2025 EBITDA in the region of GBP 170m, one source said.

The events organiser generated around GBP 430m in revenue in the fiscal year ending 31 January 2024, according ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0UstuKjkQ_Zr2rlG5_Gh64QWEIZORwmzIAnZuuxoc-nVtNwr5-itIdJXN3Viy5fOoc8q6OYb0lii-eKPWa4VyheVyvdqUUgKU9dOmLjmuucIlr2CpmZ2mLjibwziYYcyh_b4k5mLIFIP916azEdJB1Tjuq1ZUS-UrDa2qrAaJjWx4zdzc5TnS0-jJ0FA-r5k3HkSjmQ9pstmdyW9sJoOAqgRdotiDLsRKycexEFIcGRleKdCa61oyGq6mC1diZ8PBOr3kaEF7rIBrjVhRU3mvXVNVjoUHL2gUoJVUciFrBCXapRV1U3EhCgk9xRPF3sYL5YUbexbSnlI2re0Ssc6cc55SIVYFbgvctmHwpR18OU_eZroDJjvcyjC0Y-wfGS0SxWtwtDiN18V8KXD7_anALYcapKzhwdSF4VSeQ8pjvLH-HsaLN__vX_C4f1PH_ava4UEc3_8Rx_eDfH3edQd847v3y-fu879w2F8KsfmC7W8TGR9OlDKb4uhnl83Pse6Pbejo3n7doPVKWV-DBgCO2glAZL9mirdHqRqcII9EgKpeclRCOycbYWXtoOEti8YOPlJaRAqnMrlzH3wuJJwp2o_JxjxQTI8os_mjXIjNX7Uz9VNn893fT9tlpo_M5q-1RQCuRSUUuxr8HQAA__8zxeNL ) to its most recent Companies House filing. This compared to around GBP 257m in the previous 12 months.

Asia made up around 36% of the group‚Äôs revenue in the year to January 2024, followed by the US with 35%. The remaining 28% was generated out of Europe, the filing shows. A year earlier, the Asia portion was just 23% while the US accounted for 44% of the top line.

Some potential bidders voiced concerns over Clarion‚Äôs exposure to China, as well as broader geopolitical trends such as economic de-globalisation and rising conflict, which they believe may dampen demand for international business travel, one source said.

Blackstone, PAI, CVC and ICG declined to comment. Goldman Sachs, Clarion and FountainVest did not respond to requests for comments.

49. NPM Capital in exclusivity with Elbfrost as auction of wholesale fast food distributor nears end

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ NPM beats out rivals FSN, A&M in competitive auction
‚Ä¢ Discussions for c.5x unitranche financing package ongoing

Details:
NPM Capital is in exclusivity to acquire Elbfrost, a German frozen food distributor and wholesaler, from current owner Bencis Capital, two sources familiar with the situation said.

The Netherlands-based sponsor has edged past a handful of other private equity firms, including FSN and Alvarez & Marsal Capital (A&M), becoming the frontrunner for the asset in a competitive auction, the first source and a third source familiar said.

Earlier this month, this news service reported ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0kjFv2zAQhX-NuMk43pGUNXCw4zpNgbiLMtgbRZ5iJrKkUnQa59cXdooiSxcCPODd-x7eOX9OcX6aOT0Eq9drjWqF5XK92pRKAZT13aYuJa6lxqWsYGmEm6Y-epfjONhhzLH7-5mFTzFziu67m4-WlIeq9TJUHVVLHSoDna6cAYWtamUt_LnP58R3Y2DLQ3m_FsEGoNaIEOfJZX_ksHGZLQLqEkyJ1IApaKXV7VmQooNgKysNxkhTK8HDm-3jG4ujldhJKQM5AF0x6JqkZAiy7rjzTnYi3vaCQQKjlVYLVSNo6paO6raSRIWCE6dnTieXXjkv_HgScW54zrZz_cyit8ecp7mgVYHbAreB2_w7Jl7EcXCD6y85-vkqK3DrxyHzkAvcSgCFWlWaxOka8iHYn80DHponfWge9Q73dHj5RoeXvXq83_V7fJK7l9eP3cePuG9eC9p8yprLxDbEZ56zmNIYzj7br7jXYRd7vrZat-iC1i7UYABAovEEiOLXmdPlVpYBTxyQGVDXS4majPeqJadqD63sRLJuCInnReL4XM7-eIohFwqOnNz75FIeON2yimz_ORe0-a935tPUu3zl-4pdZn7P4vx5jgggDVWkxZvFPwEAAP__YHfUMA ) that NPM was among a handful of late-stage bidders, including FSN and IK Partners, circling the firm ahead of confirmatory offers. Sellside advisor Harris Williams is marketing the business off EUR 17m‚ÄìEUR 19m in EBITDA for 2024, as reported.

NPM is in discussions with private credit firms to procure unitranche financing for its acquisition of Elbfrost, the first two sources said. The sponsor is looking to line up two or three debt funds for buyout financing, the first source added.

Lenders are offering to lever the firm at around or slightly above 5x EBITDA, although some private credit providers are pitching debt packages in the 4.5x‚Äì4.75x range, the first source said. This implies a debt package of up to EUR 85m‚ÄìEUR 95m based off the marketed EBITDA.

Pricing for the unitranche could land at around 500bps over the reference rate, the first source added.

While not the most interesting company with its focus on frozen food, financiers generally see Elbfrost as a great lending case due to its size, stability and reliable cashflows, the first source said.

The firm also posts decent margins of around 13% and has a sticky customer base of institutions like hospitals and cafeterias, as reported ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0UsFu4zoM_Brr5oAiJdk-6JA0L319QPMu7iG5yRLdqHVsr6x02379Iuli0cteCJDAcGY4dP6S4vK0cHoIVm82GtUay3qz3pZKAZTN3bYpJW6kxlpWUBvh5nmI3uU4jXaccux_N4vwKWZO0f3rlpMl5aHqvAxVT1WtQ2Wg15UzoLBTnWyEvwz5kvhuCmx5LO83ItgA1BkR4jK77E8cti6zRUBdgimRWjAFrbW6lRUpOgq2stJgjDSNEjy-2SG-sTjZYCioYKgGT6y91kja9VJXDKCpBhFve8EggdFKq5VqEDT1taOmqyRRoeDM6ZnT2aVXzis_nUVcWl6y7d2wsBjsKed5KWhd4K7AXeAu_4yJV3Ea3eiGjxz9coUVuPPTmHnMBe4kgEIFDRpxvpp8CPb_9gGP7ZM-to96jwc6vvxDx5eDerzfDwd8kvuX18_953_x0L4WtP2CtR8z2xCfecliTlO4-Gy_y70O-zjwNdWmQxe0dqEBAwASjSdAFD8unD5uYZnrlQIyA-qmlqjJeK86cqrx0MleJOvGkHhZJY7P5eJP5xhyoeDEyb3PLuWR082ryPYPc0Hbv3JnPs-Dy1d932WXmd-zuHy9IwJIQxVp8WbxVwAAAP__kYvTsA ) . Some financiers declined the credit, however, as the business is somewhat commoditised with its lack of branded products and a clear-cut USP (unique selling proposition), the third source said.

Bencis has been invested in Elbfrost since 2022, according to its website. Elbfrost is a food wholesaler and logistics provider specialising in frozen products for commercial kitchens, including caterers, business canteens, hospitals, care centres and educational institutions. It operates across three sites in Germany and has a product portfolio including vegetables, chicken, fish and convenience food.

FSN declined to comment. NPM Capital, A&M, Harris Williams, Bencis Capital and Elbfrost did not respond to requests for comment.

51. SIS Swiss International School Group to acquire Colegio Suizo de Madrid

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Full integration expected by 1 September 2026
‚Ä¢ Cuatrecasas, Niederer Kraft Frey advised SIS
‚Ä¢ Financial terms not disclosed

Details:
SIS Swiss International School Group has entered into a strategic alliance with Colegio Suizo de Madrid, according to a 19 June statement from legal advisor Cuatrecasas.

The Madrid-based private school is expected to fully integrate into the SIS Group by 1 September 2026.

Financial details of the agreement were not disclosed.

SIS operates bilingual private schools across Switzerland, Germany, Brazil and Italy, offering education from kindergarten to secondary level.

Cuatrecasas advised SIS on the deal alongside Swiss law firm Niederer Kraft Frey (NKF).

52. BT‚Äôs break-up option, Stora Enso considers forestry spin, Metro Bank takeover interest ‚Äì Europe Morning Flash - Analysis

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ BT Openreach separation could unlock value
‚Ä¢ Stora Enso reviews EUR 5.8bn forestry spin
‚Ä¢ Metro Bank shares gain after takeover report

Details:
Break-up and takeover possibilities around London-listed telco BT Group appear to be gaining traction.

Allison Kirkby, CEO of the business, indicated BT may consider a spin-off of broadband unit Openreach once it completes the roll-out of its full fibre network, potentially as early as next year, according to a Financial Times report last weekend (15 June).

While BT is not actively pursuing a spin-off of the unit, it could explore the option if Openreach‚Äôs value is not appropriately reflected in BT‚Äôs share price, Kirkby said.

( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0Urtu4zAQ_Bqxk7F8SipY2HGcS4A4jVLYHUWuLCZ6HUkFSb7-IOdwcHMNAQ52d2Zn1tgl-PgaMTw6LXc7ycSW5eVuu8-FAMiru32VU7ajkpW0gFIRM8-9tyb5adTjlHz79xOJDT5h8OaXiZ3mwkLRWOqKlheldIWCVhZGgWCNaGhF7NKnJeDd5FDjmD_siNMOeKOI83E2yXbo9iahZsBkDipnvAaV8a0U12fDBT8T1LSQoBRVlSA4fujefyDptHCC07KCommMpZZi2bRQQOMkIm8FJ_46FxTjoKSQYiMqBpK3peFVU1DOMwEDhguGwYR3TBs7DcTHGmPSrekjkl53Kc0x49uMHTJ2sG7cDMPFGtvhZsSUsQM6n6bgTZ_baUw4rtgqMGMHN9llwDHlAecprmVfN2jGDi-l29Xj_cvTTIbVjUenX-pHdq5f5bl-lkd24ue3e35-O4nnh2N_Yq_0-Pb-ffx-8qf6PeP7n7b6a0bt_AVjInOY3GKTvt1rBVvf4xp_1TDjpDSuAgUAlCnLgTHye8HwdU1VgeXoGCIwWZWUSa6sFQ03orLQ0JYEbUYXMG4C-ksebTd4lzIBHQbzOZuQRgzx6mXS_5gzvv8vd8Jh7k1a9d3KzhN-JrL83C0DoIoXXJIPzf4EAAD__7kA5Kc )

The Morning Flash has been tracking takeover and break-up possibilities around BT for several years, most recently in September last year ( https://notifications.mergermarket.com/c/eJx0Uk1z4joQ_DXWzdRo9GHroAOER15eVXgXcoCbLI1BiTFeSUCSX78F2d3KZS9TNV3V0z3T4_w5xfySKT0FqxYLhXKOdbuYL2spAWrzsDQ1xwVX2PIGWs3cNA3RuxJPox1PJfa_msx8ioVSdP-6fLBCemg6z0PTi6ZVodHQq8ZpkNjJjhvmz0M5J3o4BbI01o8LFmwA0WkWYp5c8QcKS1fIIqCqQdcoNqArMVfyXmZCih0jyxsFWnNtJKPxYod4IXawCqXxElqnBVetaUTXe2NabYRrVONaFu9zQaMAraSSM2kQlOhbJ0zXcCEqCUdKe0pHl96ozPzpyGLeUC62d0MmNthDKVOuxLzCVYWr6_U6C-SGRNMpFUo3RoWrOBYahrin0VOFq0uk62_UH3Od-uu1QXa8LfwU7P-bJ9xtXtRu86zWuBW713_E7nUrnx_XwxZf-Pr17XP9-V_cbt4qsfyibT4msiHuKRc2pVM4-2K_W7-BfRzolrDp0AWlXDCgAYCj9gIQ2Y8zpY97cBq8oIBEgMq0HJXQ3stOOGk8dLxnyboxJMqzRHFfZ384xlAqCQdK7n1yqYyU8v1cxf5RrsTyr9qFjtPgys3fd9t1offCzl-viQBci0YodrH4MwAA___aXNmR ) , because of a sum-of-the parts discount centred upon Openreach.

Estimates for Openreach‚Äôs value have varied widely in media reports over the past couple of years but most have pointed to a valuation higher than BT‚Äôs current market cap of GBP 19bn.

That valuation opportunity has attracted the attention of a variety of strategic investors.

Bharti Enterprises, an industrial conglomerate backed by India‚Äôs Mittal family, acquired a 24.5% stake in BT last year from French telecoms mogul Patrick Drahi.

Deutsche Telekom owns a 12% stake, a shareholding it received in part-consideration for the mobile network EE, which BT acquired for GBP 12.5bn during 2015.

And Mexican telco entrepreneur Carlos Slim upped his stake to 4%, from 3.2%, late last year.

All three investors are likely to be watching developments closely.

A prospective spin of Openreach is likely to provide a major valuation catalyst for BT and could flush out bid interest as a result.

Shares in BT closed at 191 pence yesterday (19 June), up 4% since the report on Sunday.

Stora Enso considers partial spin-off of forestry assets

Stora Enso has kicked off a strategic review of the forestry assets, which cover approximately 1.2m hectares of forest land and had a fair value of EUR 5.8bn as of 31 March 2025.

The review is being conducted to increase shareholder value by unlocking the full potential of both its forestry and industrial packaging assets.

A break-up might also put Stora Enso in the takeover spotlight in an actively consolidating packaging sector.

Stora Enso plans to provide an update on the strategic review by the end of 2025.

Its R shares gained about 15% over the last couple of days following the announcement and closed at EUR 9.70 for a total market cap of EUR 7.7bn.

Metro Bank shares spike after reported Pollen Street interest

Could London-listed Metro Bank become the next takeover target in an ongoing consolidation of banks across the UK and Europe?

Shares in the lender spiked as much as 18% on Monday (16 June) to 133 pence following a Sky News report that it had received a takeover approach from financial sponsor Pollen Street Capital.

Metro Bank‚Äôs stock price pared some of those gains later in the week to close yesterday at 126 pence for a market cap of GBP 847m, up 12% on the week through Thursday‚Äôs close.

53. Etihad Airways drops out of Air Europa bid - report (translated)

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Lufthansa, Air France-KLM, Turkish Airlines finalising bids for Air Europa stake
‚Ä¢ Binding proposals due early July, extension possible
‚Ä¢ Etihad drops out despite European expansion interest

Details:
Etihad Airways has dropped out of the bidding for a stake in Spain-based Air Europa, El Economista reported citing unnamed market sources.

The UAE national airline, which in the initial phase was one of the favourites, has decided not to go ahead despite its interest in expanding to the European continent, the sources said.

Following this exit, the process is now down to three contenders: Lufthansa, Air France-KLM and Turkish Airlines, which are reportedly finalising their bids to take over part of the Spanish airline's capital, the item said.

The deadline for the submission of their binding proposals is early July, although an extension is not ruled out, the report said.

54. Turkish Airlines confirms non-binding talks for Air Europa

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Evaluating growth opportunities and partnership synergies with Air Europa
‚Ä¢ Air Europa valued at EUR 1bn by owner Globalia Group
‚Ä¢ Turkish Airlines to disclose updates affecting investors' decisions

Details:
Turk Hava Yollari AO (Turkish Airlines/THY) has confirmed that it is interested in the Spain-based Air Europa Holding S.L.U., and that it is holding non-binding talks to invest in the company.

There have been media reports stating that Turk Hava Yollari A.O. ("the Company") is in discussions to acquire shares in Spain-based Air Europa Holding S.L.U. ("Air Europa").

Our Company continuously evaluates growth opportunities to strengthen its position in the global aviation industry and enhance its competitiveness in the market.

In this context, as referenced in the media, non-binding discussions are being held to assess the investment opportunity in Air Europa and to explore potential partnership synergies.

In line with the Board of Directors' resolution dated 29 May 2025, the disclosure of this non-binding offer has been postponed pursuant to Article 6 of the Capital Markets Board's Communiqu√© on Material Events (II-15.1), taking into account the current stage of the process, the uncertainties involved, and the potential impact on investors' decision-making. This decision aims to protect our Company's legitimate interests and prevent any negative impact on the process. Additionally, the Board has concluded that this postponement does not pose a risk of misleading investors and has implemented the necessary measures to ensure the confidentiality of the information during the postponement period.

Should any new developments arise that could affect investors' decisions, the necessary disclosures will be shared with the public.

It had earlier been reported that Air Europa is controlled by the Globalia Group, and that the owners were valuing the airline at EUR 1bn.

55. OPTrust suspends Globalvia sale - report (translated)

Key Points:
‚Ä¢ Indicative offers from GIC, Vauban, Igneo, GIP fell short of OPTrust's expectations
‚Ä¢ Changes to shareholder rights requested by bidders for binding proposals
‚Ä¢ Globalvia valued at EUR 3bn, OPTrust's stake worth over EUR 1.2bn

Details:
OPTrust has suspended the sale of its 40.32% stake in Spanish infrastructure and mobility operator Globalvia, El Economista reported, citing knowledgeable sources.

The Canadian pension fund has decided to halt the process due to the gap between its financial expectations and the indicative offers made at the end of March by the Singapore sovereign wealth fund GIC, the French fund Vauban, the Australian fund Igneo and the US fund GIP (BlackRock), the item said.

Additionally, the funds required changes to certain rights, including pre-emptive acquisition rights, held by Globalvia's other two shareholders, PGGM and USS, to ratify their interest in binding proposals, the report said

The initial market valuation of Globalvia is close to EUR 3bn, including debt, so OPTrust's shares would reach a price of over EUR 1.2bn, the report added.
